New Basketball Techniques (4) (O)

(Not to be reprinted)

— Translated and jointly edited by Clairou Burcky, Zhang Guodong, and Qian Yiquan

The coach of the University of Arkansas has taught a reformed attacking method, in which four players insert themselves into the enemy's formation, disrupting their lines and allowing the fifth player to bring the ball into the opponent's zone and achieve complete success.

Number 4 passes the ball to Number 5. Number 5 first dribbles to the left and then turns and passes to Number 2 (Number 2 must move forward to receive the ball at this time). Numbers 1 and 3 run towards the arc of the free throw line at the same time, but the purpose of Number 1 is to block the path of Number 3's defender, allowing Number 3 to advance to the free throw area to receive Number 2's pass. Number 3 can then shoot directly or pass to Number 2 when Number 2 has escaped their defender.

The End

"New Basketball Techniques" consists of a total of forty articles, detailing the latest basketball tactics in the United States, which are very suitable for research by comrades in the Chinese basketball community. The full text has already been published. In response to readers' requests, a separate edition will be issued. — Editor's Note

Special Item

Explanation of the Ministry of Education's Reorganization of National Education in the Past Nine Months (1)

I. General Remarks

Since Qi Jiahua accepted the important task and took on the responsibility of educational administration, for the past nine months, he has been diligently following the intentions of the central government. Together with his colleagues, he has worked conscientiously to continue the efforts of his predecessors and strive for advancement. With regard to established regulations and old systems, all of which were planned and managed by his predecessors, he has not dared to make any changes easily unless they have been proven to have drawbacks through actual implementation. Therefore, all reforms have been carried out with utmost caution, gathering collective wisdom and striving to ensure that they bring more benefits than harm and are practical and easy to implement. However, within the possible scope of these reforms, Jiahua and his colleagues still hold a consistent direction, persevering and tirelessly seeking its realization. What is this direction? It is to emphasize national rejuvenation in order to vigorously reorganize and improve national education. As for the purpose of education in the Republic of China, it has been determined by the central government. However, in order to implement this purpose and enable national education to follow this purpose and achieve improvement, practical measures must be adopted to suit the times, following the purpose of education. Otherwise, even if the purpose of education has been determined, it will be difficult to expect it to benefit reality. It is believed that China must focus on national rejuvenation in education for the entire nation to be free. As for education itself, it must vigorously reorganize step by step in order for education to achieve significant results. China's national rejuvenation must rely on education in two aspects: one is to cultivate the national concept of the people, and the other is to restore the national self-confidence of the people. Dr. Sun Yat-sen once said to catch up with the world's culture and save the Chinese nation from its roots. He also said that the revival of the Chinese nation must promote national unity and restore national self-confidence. These two posthumous teachings have a consistent meaning. China must catch up with world culture, but to catch up with world culture, it must first save the Chinese nation. To save the Chinese nation, it must first promote national unity and restore national self-confidence. It is undeniable that Chinese society lacks organization and discipline. Individual freedom is regarded as common, so all elements of the group are extremely lacking. As a result, the nation is like a heap of loose sand, losing its spirit of unity and progress. If education does not take the cultivation of national concepts as its main content, it will be impossible to correct this. In recent years, China has rapidly introduced Western culture without carefully choosing it. As a result, it is busy copying and following, and eventually, any system, cultural relics, ideas, or academic theories become like oranges north of the river when they come to China. This is all due to the loss of national self-confidence. Since the people have forgotten their nation's inherent culture, they lose their autonomy in absorbing foreign culture, and they lack a foundation for creating new culture. Culture must be created, and creation must be based on inherent culture. Without this foundation, the integration of world culture has no source, and catching up with it is out of the question. If education does not take the cultivation of national self-confidence as its main content, it will be impossible to correct this. This is the purpose of improving national education by focusing on national rejuvenation. Today, the development of national education is unbalanced, and its actual content is flowing into emptiness. Higher education suffers from extravagance, while primary education is still difficult to promote. Liberal arts education suffers from parallel construction, while practical science education is still difficult to develop. Secondary schools are expanding daily, while vocational and teacher training is diminishing. Schools are concentrated in cities but lacking in rural areas. This is the imbalance in the development of national education. Schools at all levels are focused on ostentation, wasting expenses, setting up courses without focusing on the basics, lacking equipment without seeking to improve it, poor teaching leads to lower student levels, and poor moral education leads to worse school discipline. This is the emptiness of the actual content of national education. These two phenomena are also mutually reinforcing causes. Therefore, the more empty the content, the faster the development, and eventually the entire education becomes a waste and chaos. The only way to reverse this accumulated burden is to vigorously reorganize, regulate its development, so that there is a sense of urgency, and to enrich its content, so that it can be practical and effective. Otherwise, if the content is lacking and the development is deformed without correction, then each additional development will add an additional layer of error to the entire education. The more development, the greater the error, and the deeper the poisoning. All these points are the fundamental direction of the Ministry's improvement of national education. Since February of this year, all the facilities of the Ministry, whether they have been implemented successively or are still being planned separately, have been held to this purpose as a standard for selection. I will present them separately.

II. Promoting Compulsory Education and Improving Primary School Education

Building the lower-level foundation of the nation lies in the popularization of education. Compulsory education and primary school education are the key plans for the popularization of education. Any country that wants to seek the popularization of education must promote primary school education to become compulsory education. However, China's primary school education has not been well managed, and social economy and local finances are extremely impoverished. Compulsory education and primary school education cannot be combined into one. Therefore, we must fully improve primary school education and simultaneously promote compulsory education. To improve primary school education, the Ministry has already revised the Primary School Organization Law and Primary School Regulations. The Primary School Regulations include strict provisions on local education research, the organization of primary schools, the allocation of funds, the enrichment of equipment, the reform of moral education, and the treatment and training of teachers. In particular, the curriculum has been issued detailed standards, with special emphasis, in order to enable existing primary schools to follow these various regulations and enrich their content with scientific methods. As for compulsory education, the Ministry has promulgated the General Outline of Measures for Implementing Compulsory Education in the First Phase and the General Outline of Measures for Implementing Short-Term Compulsory Education. The Measures for Implementing Compulsory Education in the First Phase stipulate that junior primary schools are compulsory education, in order to gradually implement it by year and region, first with experiments and then with promotion, so that in the future, junior primary schools will be universally established and become compulsory education. At present, there are more than 30 million out-of-school children aged ten to sixteen in China. If they are all to receive four years of compulsory junior primary school education, not only will the annual funding of 300 million yuan be impossible to raise, but also the 1.4 million primary school teachers cannot be trained in a hurry. Therefore, it is necessary to divide the years and regions, experiment and promote it, and gradually seek to establish it universally. However, this method alone is not enough to meet the urgent need. Therefore, the Measures for Implementing Short-Term Compulsory Education is also used to provide urgent relief to a large number of out-of-school children. This method shortens the compulsory education period to one year of short-term primary school, using a purely class-based system, so that out-of-school children aged ten to sixteen who are busy working and farming can also take time to study. The curriculum aims to literacy, and only sets up one type of national language, including common sense numeracy, making it particularly simple. Therefore, the Measures for Implementing Compulsory Education in the First Phase defines compulsory education as four years, which is intended to gradually promote it, making it easy to increase to six years and then increase to more than six years, in order to show a permanent plan. The Measures for Implementing Short-Term Compulsory Education temporarily sets one year as short-term compulsory education, which is intended to make it universally established, making it easy to implement compulsion, in order to meet the urgent need. At present, the number of out-of-school students in the country is too large, and national affairs are deteriorating daily. The promotion of compulsory education cannot be allowed to be leisurely delayed. We must gradually promote it without making other urgent remedies.

Securities and Short-Term Finance Market Opened Yesterday

All Bonds Showed a Rebound

The Trend Was Very Chaotic

Yesterday (the 5th), in the bond market of the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange, only the current month of the 20-year financial short-term public bonds opened. Transactions were scarce and the price was very high. The popularity of other bonds in the morning and afternoon markets was still quite active, but there were only scattered spot transactions. The bond trend was very chaotic, with some rising and others falling, and large fluctuations. There was no consistent trend between the different trading sessions. The overall situation was dull and there were no new developments in the environment. Although there were many transactions, people's minds were unsettled. The rise and fall of prices only shifted with the temporary supply and demand situation in the market. Buying interest once again dominated the situation, with a rebound compared to the previous week. Bonds such as Disarmament, Taxes, Consolidated Tax, and 20 Customs rose by more than one yuan each, while others rose by about half a yuan. Due to the lack of recent transactions, spot trading for 6% and Tax bonds fell significantly. Futures trading totaled 5.6 million in the morning and over 3.8 million in the afternoon, totaling 9,415,000 yuan. Spot trading totaled 26,000 yuan.

New York Stock Market Continues to Fall

According to a report from a New York firm, the New York stock market on Saturday (the 3rd) initially declined due to the weakness of the British pound, but rebounded due to a good freight report. The number of freight cars during the week totaled 493,882, a decrease of 81,969 compared to the previous week, likely due to the Thanksgiving holiday. However, it was still considered good compared to last year. There were no changes in the war debt issue, which was basically whether or not to pay. According to the current stock market situation, it has approached the support line created between October and November. Some selling occurred last week due to the war debt issue, but the selling pressure was not strong, so the decline was also weak. Major holders clearly did not want to sell hastily, expecting the situation to improve in the future and the market to rise. Therefore, although the current situation is poor, it seems unnecessary to sell. If one holds blue-chip stocks, such as ordinary shares of Diamond Match and preferred shares of General Motors, there is even a reason to buy. The Dow Jones indices are listed below:

Yarn and Cotton Yarn Market Mostly Dumping

Yarn Warehouse Inventory Reaches 8,9000 Bales

The cotton yarn market was weak in the morning and firm in the afternoon, but the trend was still scattered, with no sign of recovery. Due to the deterioration of the environment, the actual demand in the market was stagnant, and various promotions were ineffective, leading to widespread fatigue and a tendency to sell. However, some, due to their small base, did not dare to dump excessively. According to a survey of yarn and cloth warehouses, there are reportedly 89,000 bales of 20-count yarn of the "Ren Zhong Cai Hua," "San Yang," and "Fu Gui" brands. With such a huge amount of inventory, the pressure on the yarn market is increasing.

Ren Biao (Cotton Futures) Market Slightly Settled in the Afternoon

The Ren Biao market opened lower in the morning due to the further decline of American cotton. The sentiment in the market was more cautious, with prices falling by 5-6 cents across various months. A rebound was seen in the second and third trading sessions, resulting in a decrease of 2-5 cents across various months. In the afternoon, some profit-takers covered their short positions, and the market sentiment slightly calmed, with prices rising by 1-3 cents across various months. The total volume of transactions for the day was 16,200 bales. Yi Chang sold 1,350 bales, Yu Yu 900 bales, and Sui Jiang 600 bales. Shen Xin bought 750 bales, Shen Ji 700 bales, Tong He 550 bales, Yong Ren 350 bales, and Da Chang 350 bales. The closing prices are listed below:

Cotton Market Situation Still Stable

Arrivals are Scarce, Prices are Firm

Not Influenced by Foreign Cotton

The cotton market experienced a weakening trend due to the further decline of American cotton and the increasing decline of Indian cotton. However, as the arrival of goods from various regions was limited and there were not many new sellers in the market, and prices in Hankou, Tianjin, Jinan, Zhengzhou, and other places were difficult to lower, the current domestic cotton market remained high despite the decline in overseas markets. However, due to the financial emergency and the fatigue of the yarn market, factories had no intention of making large-scale purchases, so the overall trend remained a sideways market.

Zheng Biao (Cotton Futures) Market Initially Soft, Then Recovered

The Zheng Biao market opened lower in the morning, with the decline in the American and Indian markets causing a slight downturn in market sentiment. Prices fell by 1 cent across various months. In the afternoon, there were reports that some factories purchased more than 1,000 pieces of spot cotton, causing the market situation to tighten slightly. Prices rose by 0.5-1 cent across various months. The total volume of transactions for the day was 29,600 dan. Da Feng sold 2,800 dan, Sheng Tai 2,500 dan, Rong Xing 1,300 dan, and Chang He 1,200 dan. Yi Chang bought 1,000 dan, Yi Yu 1,100 dan, Da Chang 1,300 dan, Yuan Xing Chang 2,400 dan, and Yi Feng 1,200 dan. The closing prices are listed below:

Foreign Cotton Uniformly Declines

Yesterday, American cotton declined due to unfavorable news from Liverpool. Foreign merchants sold, and selling pressure caused the market to weaken. Futures fell by 6-12 points, and spot goods fell by 5 points. British cotton futures fell by 12 points, and spot goods fell by 16 points. Egyptian cotton spot goods fell by 22 points. Indian cotton weakened due to unfavorable news from Liverpool and profit-taking by bulls. Ping Guo Er fell by 6.75 rupees, Om La fell by 6.5 rupees, and Bai Luo Xi fell by 6.25 rupees. Indian Cotton Sales Still Smooth

│Silver Price Drop Benefits Exports│

(Bombay) The gap between Indian and American prices widened further last week, benefiting exports, due to the drop in silver prices. Japanese merchants purchased futures cotton, mainly Om La. The Japanese purchases are the main reason for maintaining the Indian-American price difference. Besides Japan, the demand for Indian cotton is minimal. Local factories are also weak. The weather is unstable, but it benefits Om La. New cotton arrivals are delayed due to the shipment of Indian gold to America. (Liverpool) Spot demand remained unchanged last week. Futures declined due to political factors and the weakness of Egyptian cotton. The amount of profit-taking and hedging could not be fully absorbed by the industry. Therefore, even with the low silver prices, it could only maintain the status quo. Egyptian cotton weakened due to unfavorable news from American cotton and Asia.

Grain and Rice Market Rises by One Dime

(Hu Nan) Yesterday, there were not many sources from various groups due to the wind and rain, only about 30 suppliers. The inventory in Pu Dong was also substantial. Tianjin-based merchants purchased 2,000 bags of "Bao Zi" rice for several consecutive days, pushing the situation upwards. Early rice and northern japonica rice both rose by about one dime. High-quality "Yang Jian" rice was sold at the same price, with no rise or fall. Although the supply of "Yin Hua" rice was limited, the liquor stores were satisfied, and the price remained stable.

(Xin Guan) Yesterday, there were not many sources from the west road, about 55-60 suppliers. There was limited activity in the morning due to light rain. Changshu northern japonica rice and Jiangyin rice were quoted up by one dime. The interest in thin rice was slightly active, with nearly 1,000 shi (unit of volume) of riverbed rice being traded.

Ke Xian (Rice) Supply Will Exceed Demand

│Arrivals Gradually Increase… Fujian Merchants' Appetite Remains Strong│

│After Du Rice is Exported North… Foreign Rice May Have a Chance│

Yesterday, the Ke Xian market was active and sales were strong. The market seemed to be on the path to a lively state. However, as arrivals exceeded sales, prices tended to decline. Yesterday, new arrivals of Ke Yuan and Ke Xian rice from Anhui and Hunan provinces totaled around 5,000 bags, with only half being sold. Therefore, although the market sentiment was good, the price declined by about one dime. Ke Yuan was especially weaker due to the influence of new riverbed rice and rice stored from Jiangxi machine rice mills. Wu machine rice was previously sold at a high of 10 yuan and 7.5 jiao and 11 yuan. Last week, it was still quoted at 10 yuan. Yesterday, it fell to below 9 yuan, a decrease of 1.5 jiao. Anqing machine rice, with lower quality, was even weaker. The unified market price for 770 bags of Wu machine rice was 9 yuan and 9 jiao to 8.5 jiao. 270 bags of Anqing machine rice were priced at 8 yuan and 2.5 jiao to 2 jiao. 150 bags of Jiangxi late rice were priced at 8 yuan and 3 jiao. 1,000 bags of Hunan "Yan Jing" rice were priced at 7 yuan and 3.9 jiao to 2.5 jiao. 300 bags of Hunan "Po Hong" rice were priced at 7 yuan to 6 yuan and 9 jiao. Among them, the Jiangxi machine late rice was purchased by merchants from Quanzhou, Fujian province. The remaining rice was purchased by merchants from Fujian province. The appetite of Fujian merchants remained strong, and it was necessary to continue active purchases. However, Northern merchants, due to the potential for export of Du japonica rice from this province and Zhejiang, shifted their attention. In the future, the export of Ke Xian rice to the north may disappear. Ke Xian arrivals gradually increased, but sales relied solely on Fujian merchants. There was a risk of oversupply. However, after the export of Du japonica rice to the north, the sales of foreign rice in this street may have a new lease of life.

Biao Fen (Flour) Hovers with a Softening Trend

│Heard Large Factories Agreed to Purchase Two More Shipments of Coast Wheat│

After the flour market opened yesterday morning, the market for various months initially showed a tired and then stable trend. As foreign wheat prices declined by about one dime, the market sentiment was not good when the opening prices were quoted. Near-term prices were lower by about 0.5%. However, as factories were not selling well and outside sentiment remained good, it stabilized again. When the market opened in the afternoon, the market for various months hovered and began to show a softening trend. Tianjin merchants continued to sell out, and Australian foreign wheat was recently active again. It was heard that large factories agreed to purchase two more shipments at prices ranging from 3 taels and 5 qian to 3 taels, 5 qian, 3-4 fen. Xin Da has newly arrived with over 3,000 tons of foreign wheat. It seems that current production can already meet demand, so the market sentiment gradually weakened. The future rise and fall will depend on how actual sales perform. As a result, the current month remained unchanged, while prices for January and February fell by 0.25%, and prices for March, April, and May fell by 0.5%.

Futures Wheat Remains On The Sidelines

│Soon Foreign Wheat Will Be Imported in Large Quantities│

│The Position of Domestic Wheat Will Inevitably Be Shaken│

Yesterday, after the futures wheat market opened in the afternoon, the market for various months again tended to hover. Foreign wheat prices showed little fluctuation. Buyers and sellers remained on the sidelines. Trading was unusually scarce in the morning. The afternoon was slightly busier. February and March initially showed firmness. It was reported that there were new transactions of foreign wheat, and the price fell by 0.2 fen. There were very few transactions in April, and the market tended to stabilize. With the imminent large-scale import of foreign wheat, the position of domestic wheat would inevitably be shaken. As a result, only April was slightly better by 0.1 fen, with no comparison for the others.

Chicago Wheat Bulls Take Profits

According to a report from Xin Feng Foreign Firm, Chicago wheat on Saturday (the 3rd) initially rose due to the poor condition of the Argentine wheat crop, but then fell due to profit-taking by bulls. A total of 3,000 bushels were traded on the 2nd. The market prices for the 2nd are listed below:

Sugar Market Domestic Qing Sugar Transactions Still Numerous

The sugar market yesterday saw a stabilization of the trend with the decline in the Biao Jin (tariff). The association's market price for Grade 24 coarse sand white common sugar was initially 15 taels and 6 qian, which later dropped to 5 qian and 7.5 fen, with hundreds of bags transacted. The price of high-grade sugar was 15 taels and 7 qian, the price of Grade 20 medium sand white sugar was 14 taels and 8 qian, and the price of Grade 18 medium sand white sugar was 14 taels and 5 qian, with little fluctuation. The market for Dutch red sugar remained tight, with Grade 8 sugar priced at 11 taels and 6.5 qian to 7 qian, Grade 9 sugar at 11 taels and 8 qian, and Grade 10 sugar at 11 taels and 9 qian. Merchants from Guangdong offered 900 pieces of secondary Qing sugar at a price of 8 taels per bag and 15 taels and 3.5 qian. Merchants from Shantou offered over 1,000 bags of Mian Hu red sugar over the past two days at a price of 11 taels, and secondary sugar at 10 taels and 6 qian. Merchants from Jian offered dozens of boxes of high-grade hand-made ice sugar, with each block priced at 10 taels and 2 qian.

Silk and Tea

Zhen Mei Green Tea Sales Slightly Active in France

Yesterday, the Zhen Mei green tea from Lu Zhuang and Tu Zhuang and other areas saw slightly more active sales in France. However, the opening market prices for tea from Tunxi were 70 taels within the customs, and the price for tea from Wenzhou and Yushan was 31-32 taels, a further decline of 2-3 taels compared to before. There was little progress for tea from Yiyuan. There was some interest in Gong Xi, with High Zhuang and Low Zhuang tea, Bai Tou Zhuang, Qian Yi Yu Jiang, and other firms all showing interest. Transactions were not quiet. However, there were no transactions in the Middle Customs tea because Russian firms had excessively harsh prices.

Free Talk

Short Stories

Newlywed Night (5)

— Bing Xin

"What is there to be ashamed of? I simply won't go in. See what you can do? I haven't stolen a man or robbed anyone's belongings. What am I afraid of?"

This was truly beyond Aunt's expectations. She never imagined Miss Xiu would have such courage.

"Don't make a scene. You're not a child of three or five. Every woman has to marry."

Aunt's voice deliberately lowered a bit.

"Hmph! Why must I marry? Can't I live on my own? Even if I were to marry, which I won't for life, I would marry someone I want to marry. I won't be sold off by you! Hmph! Sold to a monkey older than my father! Oh God, I'm scared, I'm terrified!..."

More and more people gathered to watch the commotion. Aunt was as anxious as an ant on a hot pan, at her wit's end. Miss Xiu was so worked up she was about to faint. Her tears had long since dried up, and suddenly a lot of fresh blood gushed from her nose.

"Quick, get some cotton!"

"It's alright, it's just the heat rising. It's not a big deal."

"This bride must have a fiery temper."

"You can't blame her. She's so pitiful, marrying such an old thing."

"Really, and so ugly!"

"And a miser who loves money more than life."

"Don't say that, shut your mouth."

"What's it to you!"

"..."

"..."

These were the noisy voices coming from the crowd.

"Aunt, thank you for being such a good matchmaker! I will die before your very eyes today! I will never go back to that old monkey. I'd rather... I'd rather die than, no, no... I don't want to see his face again!"

"Mom! Your efforts have been in vain. I will never yield, I will resist to the end! My life cannot be sold off by you, cannot be handed over to others to be slaughtered. I will dispose of myself, destroy myself..."

With a "bang," Miss Xiu slammed her head against the wall. The back of her head happened to hit a very small nail, only half an inch long, and blood spurted out like a waterfall. The crowd screamed in horror. Some sighed and shed tears of sympathy, while others rubbed their fists by the window, writing in big letters: "Damn old monkey, killing such a young and beautiful girl!"

Miss Xiu's blood continued to flow. The doctor had not yet arrived, and she had already fainted.

Afternoon, November 28, 1932

"Note 1": This is a dialect from Xinhua, Hunan. The first time a virgin has relations with a man is called "yuan fang".

"Note 2": A "stone woman" is a virgin whose physical structure is incomplete, making it impossible to have sexual relations with a man.

"Note 3": This describes the meaning of a beautiful woman marrying an ugly husband.

"Note 4": This says that older men know how to cherish their wives, while young people treat their wives as unimportant as grass.

About Clothes

— Jing

Lately, when going to the bathhouse, I dread the attendant taking off my clothes the most. Although my suit, made five years ago, still looks like a garment on the outside, the inside is tattered and frayed. Even I feel embarrassed when I see it. My clothes are like this, so you can imagine my life. My friend T even wrote to me saying that I "imitate the bourgeoisie at sea in the ranks of the proletariat," which is truly an injustice!

Having spent so many years in society, and ending up like this, not even having proper clothes, you must criticize me, saying, "This is either too incompetent, or too lazy, definitely not contributing to society!" For me, perhaps that's all appropriate. I am willing to accept it. However, what about those skilled craftsmen, those farmers who toil like cattle and horses all day long, those soldiers who take a few dollars a month, or even nothing at all, and exchange their lives for a living? Are they useful materials? Are they hardworking individuals? Are their clothes adequate? I'm afraid having a tattered garment that can keep out the cold is already a great comfort! Can you put on a stern face and say, "Definitely not contributing to society?"

Or you might change your tune and say, "Their abilities are too limited." Really? Not so! What does "limited ability" mean? Those who amass the wealth of the people, those who swallow public funds and money, depositing entire batches of banknotes in foreign banks, spending snow-white silver dollars like flowing water, can this be called "great ability?" And those who inherit large estates, unable to carry anything on their shoulders or lift anything with their hands, useless in all things, yet they never worry about what to wear in winter or what to change into in summer: can this also be called "having ability?" Society is like this, can you say it's none of your business?

If you still insist on saying that it has nothing to do with society, then I have nothing to say. I can only blame myself for "being born at the wrong time," not being born as a rich or noble person, or the descendants of the rich, or the wives and concubines of the noble! Otherwise, I can only blame myself for "being born in the wrong place," not being born in the tropics, where a single pair of trousers can be worn year-round. However, even there, there are many poor people who can't even afford that one pair of trousers!

Moving

— Xingzi

Yesterday, I moved again. For the past half year, my wife has been constantly making a fuss about moving, saying either that there are too many bedbugs or that the mosquitoes are annoying. So we move back and forth, moving away and then moving back.

Thinking about it, I can't help but laugh. Every time we move, I always say to my friends in this way or that way: "This house is so bad! I can't stand the bedbugs and mosquitoes!" And the new house is so good... I've said this more than once. At first, my friends would nod, expressing agreement. Now they're used to it and don't pay much attention no matter how enthusiastically I speak. I think moving is always good, because moving, to put it nicely, is a change of residence. Although bedbugs and mosquitoes don't break off relations with me just because I move, the two lines of poetry, "Coming from a secluded valley, moving to a tall tree," are, after all, so pleasing and sweet.

Speaking of moving, I'm reminded of two stories. One is "Mother Meng moved three times," but my little daughter is only four months old and not as mischievous as A Ke. Also, I don't expect the world to have another "Sage," so moving back and forth like Mother Meng seems unnecessary.

The second is that Duke Gu Danfu initially lived in Bin, but when the Di people invaded, he moved the entire nation to the foot of Mount Qi. Those who followed him were like those returning to the market. This was a vast and mighty relocation. But what harms this small child is only bedbugs and mosquitoes. And the only one who follows is a four-month-old daughter. I dare not presume to compare myself, and besides, this is a "matter of state," not something I should concern myself with. So, this can also be dismissed!

Since I don't want to compare myself to Mother Meng, and I don't dare to presume to imitate Duke Gu Danfu... Then what...? So, I remembered the saying from my hometown, "Monkeys moving their young." Good, let's just say it's "Monkeys moving their young!"

The Eastward Deflection of Objects Falling from High Places

— Sheng

Between 1546 and 1601 AD, the Danish astronomer Tycho Brahe denied the Earth's rotation. He said: "If the Earth truly rotates from west to east, then objects falling from high places must fall slightly to the west of the point below." But at the time, no one could discover this phenomenon of falling objects deflecting westward. Later, in 1679, Newton and Hooke corresponded with each other to discuss this matter. As a result, falling objects deflected not westward but eastward. The first person to experimentally prove the eastward deflection of falling objects was the Italian physicist Guglielmini. In 1792, at the Tower of Degli Asinelli in Bologna (240 feet high), he dropped sixteen spheres, all of which landed slightly to the east.

Also, the German physicist Benzenberg, in 1802, dropped thirty-one spheres from the tower of St. Michael's Church in Hamburg (over 340 feet high). Eleven of them landed four lines to the east, which is about two minutes and seven li. The following year, he conducted this experiment in the vertical shaft of the Schlesebusch coal mine near Sprockhosvel. In 1831, the physicist Reich conducted 106 trials in the vertical shaft (about 480 feet deep) of the Dreibrüder in Freiberg, Saxony. All the spheres fell to the east. The average distance from the original position was twelve lines and two-fifths (about eight minutes and two li).

From the above experiments, it is known that the eastward deflection of falling objects is an undeniable fact. The reason for this, of course, is the Earth's rotation.

Nurseries in Soviet Russia

— Ke Duo

Since Soviet Russia created a new system of government, many new things have emerged in society in the past eleven years. Now, when women in Soviet Russia have babies, they no longer need to hire wet nurses, or mix formula, or wash diapers. They simply send their newborns to the state-run nurseries, where nurses and nannies in white coats and white hats will raise them.

Nurseries are called "Yaslin" in Russian. Some translate it as "infant homes". In today's Soviet cities and villages, nurseries have been established in places with large populations.

These nurseries are either specially built or attached to workers' dormitories, large libraries, playgrounds, and clubs. They are always well-lit, well-ventilated, and designed according to scientific methods to ensure that children are in good health.

Generally, the nursery facilities begin with a small infant reception and dispatch room. This room is specifically for families to rest when dropping off and picking up infants. When parents bring their infants to the nursery, they first hand them over to a caregiver, who removes all their clothing, leaving not a single thread, and places the clothing in a closet about four feet high and five to six feet long. This small closet is divided into many small compartments, each of which is further divided into upper and lower compartments. The upper compartment is larger, and the lower compartment is smaller. Hats and clothing are placed in the upper compartment, and pants, socks, and shoes are placed in the lower compartment. Next to each compartment, the infant's name is written. One compartment is for one infant, and it is never mixed up. After these procedures are completed, the infant is taken to the examination room to be checked by a doctor for any illnesses. If there are any illnesses, the infant is sent to the ward. The ward is also divided into rooms for mild and severe illnesses. If the infant's illness is very serious, then the parents take them back and send them to the hospital for diagnosis and treatment. Infants without illnesses are placed in the common infant residence.

The sanitary facilities in the nursery are very complete, with medicine rooms, examination rooms, light illness rooms, and rooms for suspected illnesses. Infants with coughs and colds are not housed with healthy infants, but are placed in separate rooms. In the children's playroom, they play in groups according to their age, each group in a separate room with no more than eleven or twelve children, and a caregiver is specially assigned to manage them.

The bedrooms are also divided into two types: day bedrooms and night bedrooms. Day bedrooms usually have many windows, making it easy to absorb sunlight. Each bedroom contains fifteen or sixteen small white wire beds with railings. The beds have very clean white blankets, sheets, and mattresses. Before the infants go to sleep, they wear a sleeping garment that resembles a bag, slightly smaller at both ends and larger in the middle. After the infants fall asleep, only their heads are exposed, and all four limbs are wrapped in the bag, making it difficult for them to catch a cold. Before bedtime, the caregiver must check the thermometer to see how to open and close the small windows (because the climate in Soviet Russia is very cold, and in winter, all the windows are tightly sealed with paint and ash, with only a small window opened on the large window, which is often opened and closed to circulate air). The night bedroom is similar to the day bedroom, except that the infants wear a sleeping garment that is not a bag and is exposed to sunlight.

Infants' soiled clothing, sleeping garments, sheets, blankets, etc., are systematically washed every three days. In the summer, infants usually sleep outdoors during the day to get more sunlight. Caregivers bathe the infants every day, and the towels and soap used are separated for each person to prevent the spread of disease.

In addition to the necessary toys and bedding for infants, the walls of the bedrooms and playrooms are also decorated with pictures of animals, plants, landscapes, and so on, to create a sense of beauty for the children and cultivate a concept of art.

Children's diets have a certain time and quantity, and they are also separated according to age. The main foods are milk, eggs, and vegetables. Cooks must have the items they purchase inspected by a doctor before cooking and giving them to the children.

All staff members in the nursery wear white clothing during working hours. People who are not related are strictly prohibited from entering. People who go to the nursery to visit must also wear the white clothing provided by the nursery, and then be led in by the director or staff member, who will provide detailed explanations to the visitors.

Infants can only be raised in nurseries until the age of three. After the age of three, they must be sent to kindergarten.

Full Length Novel

Crossroads of the Era and Love

— Zhang Ziping

He pressed the doorbell at number 45 H Lane. After a while, a middle-aged man who looked like a head servant or a carriage driver, speaking with a northern accent, opened the iron gate and asked who he was. Haiquan gave him a name card and explained that he was a relative from Guangzhou. The man politely invited him into the parlor inside.

"Sir, you're early."

The handyman smiled and handed him a cup of hot tea.

"Early? It's past ten o'clock, isn't it?"

"It just rang. The young master hasn't gotten up yet..."

As the handyman spoke, he saw that the room was very dim, so he turned on the electric lights. Haiquan looked at the furnishings in the room, which were quite luxurious, especially the wallpaper, which was extraordinarily bright. But even after ten o'clock, there was no sunlight to be seen. Such a residence was like hell or a prison. The first thing people need is air, and the second is sunlight. Living in such houses, they may not be considered happy.

"Hasn't the young mistress gotten up either?"

Haiquan really wanted to see this Sister Peizhen now, to see if her face and figure resembled his beloved Peizhu.

"If I marry Peizhu, then I and that Master Ren would be in-laws."

"They only went to sleep recently."

"What? They only went to sleep?"

"Didn't they? Last night, they played mahjong until five o'clock this morning. Each person ate a bowl of chicken noodle soup and drank half a cup of Korean ginseng soup before resting."

After saying that, the handyman showed a lewd smile on his face. From this smile, Haiquan sensed the decadence of Ren's couple's life.

"Maybe Peizhen and Master Ren's relationship is still very strong right now."

Thinking of this, he couldn't help but feel his cheeks flush. At the same time, he felt extremely embarrassed.

"Well, I'll come back another day. They haven't gotten up yet. I don't want to disturb them."

"Is there anything important?"

The handyman had a Shandong accent.

"There's nothing."

As he said that, he walked towards the door. At the same time, he also envied Master Ren's couple's life. He felt a kind of contradiction.

"Playing mahjong until dawn! I really don't know what the taste of mahjong is like." He was about to walk out of the door.

"Mr. Lin, please wait a moment. The old maid just went up to serve. The young mistress said she would come down immediately and insisted that you wait a while..."

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Chinese Language Class

— Fo

This publication aims to stimulate the interest of general students in the study of Chinese and to expose the dark situation in the education community. It has a section called "School Photos," so the contributors are all top students in schools, and the materials they write are mostly romantic situations of students, and otherwise, they are nothing more than materials for joking with teachers during Chinese language classes. This is not because the authors have any particular ill feeling towards Chinese language teachers. This is a general phenomenon in schools. What a heartbreaking thing this is.

Today, I will put aside the general romantic students for the time being, and I will also talk about "Chinese Language Class." I have also eaten from the public pot and served as a Chinese language teacher in middle schools and universities for several years. Because I rely on my seniority, students dare not make trouble for me, but I carefully investigate. The students who fundamentally believe in and like to study Chinese are truly a minority of the minority. When I saw this situation, I felt very sad.

Because language is the foundation of a country, cultural aggression is the only weapon of imperialists. Therefore, if you want to destroy a country, you must first destroy its language as a primary condition. Now that other countries have a tendency to gradually culturally invade our country, our culturally backward country naturally cannot resist. However, we should not forget our ancestors and first destroy our own language. Because although there are places in our culture that are not in line with the times, language is ultimately not on the list to be discarded.

I once asked the students why they have no faith in or interest in Chinese. They have several answers as follows:

1. We come to school to study English and mathematics as our main purpose. Assuming we want to study Chinese, there are many good teachers at home, so why spend so much money to come to school.

2. English and mathematics are relatively new and pleasing, while Chinese inevitably has a stale atmosphere. Moreover, in any profession, those who are proficient in English will definitely be treated better, and those who are not proficient in English will definitely be treated worse. This is also because of environmental pressure.

3. The higher the student's level, the more serious the English and mathematics courses become. Now, devoting all our brainpower to studying English and mathematics is not enough. Where can we find the time to study Chinese?

4. The scores in Chinese are the least accurate. As long as the writing is coherent, no matter what, we can always "pass." It is not as strict as the evaluation of English and mathematics.

These few answers are not wrong at all. Because of this, students treat Chinese as a conversation class, some as a novel reading class, some as a love letter writing class, and some as a tutoring class for various courses. Their views are like this. So, can they still have faith in Chinese language teachers? Can they still refrain from making trouble? However, to remedy this problem, it is not something that one side can be responsible for. Several parties need to be responsible.

1. Chinese language teachers must study teaching methods and teaching materials to stimulate students' interest in studying Chinese.

2. The school authorities should not focus solely on English and mathematics when allocating courses. They must ensure that various subjects develop equally.

3. We must reduce various boring courses so that students can focus their minds and attention on various important subjects.

Because of the three words "Chinese Language Class," I am reminded of the decline of Chinese studies in our country. Students are unwilling to study or disdain to study Chinese, so that there are college graduates whose Chinese writing is still incoherent. Therefore, I have hastily written down some of the random feelings I have gained, as a conversation.

Literature and Art

Miscellaneous Feelings on the Kunhu Road

— Wang Fuding

A lonely city corner gathers ten thousand troops, rivers and mountains suddenly rise in wind and clouds. The heaven-supporting tree is like a strong general, with meritorious deeds of protecting the Hu in the past.

The water on Qingyang Port flows slowly, and no one can cross the hundred-foot floating bridge. The remains are full of tears, and the deep bones have endless hatred.

Important places cannot avoid enemy contention, and artillery fire ruthlessly turns tiles into rubble. A small window suddenly catches the eye, linking the vicissitudes of life to sorrowful feelings.

More than good bamboo and fertile fields have been destroyed. Sad wild geese are good to return to their dwellings after the chaos is settled. In the depths of spring, they compete to shovel the Hu ditches, and plant mulberry and hemp again, and plant vegetables again.

Science

How to Make Solid Alcohol

— Gu Lushuang

Alcohol is a liquid at room temperature and is easily volatile. It only becomes solid at 130 degrees below zero Celsius. This temperature cannot be reached without special equipment. Even if it can be made solid, it cannot last long. Therefore, it is usually impossible to make solid alcohol.

With the development of science, it is often possible to find a way out of a dead end. This solid alcohol, which has a wide range of uses (details below), cannot be obtained at room temperature, so chemists use the principles of colloid chemistry to create a new way to manufacture it and provide it to the public. The reader is very willing to know how it is made.

There are many methods for making alcohol using colloid chemistry. Now, the two most effective and convenient methods are described separately:

First method

Preparation: Pour 85 cc of 95% alcohol into a cup. Pour 15 cc of a saturated solution of calcium acetate into another cup. This saturated solution of calcium acetate is made by dissolving calcium acetate in warm water until no more can be dissolved.

Method: Take another larger cup, hold each of the above cups containing the solution with both hands, and simultaneously pour the contents into the large cup. If the speed of both hands is the same when pouring, it will become a gel-like solid alcohol. To use, simply light it and it will burn. An old cigarette can can also be used to hold the solid alcohol, but it must be closed tightly when not in use.

The product obtained by the above method has residue after burning, while the one obtained by the second method has very little.

Second method

Preparation: Put one thousand parts of 90% alcohol into a glass container, 30 parts of dry soap flakes, and 2 parts of gum.

Method: Place the above container with alcohol on boiling water. The temperature of the contents of the cup should be 63 degrees Celsius, no higher. Then, put in the soap flakes and gum, mix and harmonize to dissolve the soap completely, pour into a cigarette can, and it will become solid alcohol after cooling.

The above two methods are very convenient to make. The author has personally done them and knows that they are very effective. In the cold winter weather, alcohol has many uses, and there are also many disasters caused by alcohol overturning. If solid alcohol is used, all dangers can be avoided, and the firepower is the same as liquid alcohol, and it is convenient to carry. Travelers appreciate it very much.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Sketches of Several Teachers

— Whirlpool

Mr. Xu, the Chinese language teacher, has a comical appearance: a swarthy face set off by a mop of frizzy, curly hair; a short body lost in baggy, slovenly clothes. His scholarship is not bad; he has some research in literature, philosophy, and philology; and his music is also excellent. When lecturing, he accompanies his words with hand and foot gestures, and he tells a lot of jokes, so he is very popular with the students. Because he is skilled in music, he actually sang an excerpt from the "Peach Blossom Fan" on the podium during a lesson, making everyone laugh until they doubled over.

Mr. Chen, the English teacher, is still very young and a minor writer. He has published a magnum opus (?) and often has major works published in certain magazines, so he has the air of a literary figure. It is said that he used to be a teaching assistant at a certain university, so he has also learned the airs of a professor. After the bell rings for class, at least six or seven minutes must pass before he arrives leisurely with his large briefcase. As for his teaching method, I dare not flatter him, but because he is a writer? So students dare not despise him.

Mr. Yu, the mathematics teacher, is extremely handsome: shiny hair, a well-tailored Western suit, shiny black leather shoes... Ah, he has all the qualifications of a modern man! But, but his scholarship is too poor, especially his English proficiency is too low. Even the simplest mathematical exercises in English require him to explain them in a disjointed manner. However, he gives grades exceptionally generously, so students who "only look at grades" do not suffer. Moreover, he is very responsible; he has not missed a single class this semester, which can also be considered one of his strengths.

Mr. Zhou, the history teacher, is a teacher whom the students both respect and fear. He is a large man, and his waddling gait is quite amusing. His Mandarin is very fluent, and he tells history as if he were telling a story, making it more and more interesting to listen to, so everyone loves to attend his class. However, his exams are the most severe. His sharp gaze shines everywhere, making everyone afraid to look directly at him and afraid to cheat.

There is also a Mr. Chen, the geography teacher, who is like a virgin: extremely shy. If a student says a teasing word to him, his face immediately turns red, but he never gets angry. His voice is very soft, and he is very nearsighted. Because he is a Ningbo native, his most common phrase is "A-la." A certain mischievous student counted the number of times he said these two words in one lesson and found that it was more than forty times!

The Misfortune of the Concubines

— Wen Bing

"Mr. Ronggui, not only do you hope that the commander will soon assume a new position, but we are even more eager!" The nineteen-year-old Third Concubine, seeing Mr. He Ronggui, who was staying at the commander's house waiting for a job, with a worried face, said娇娇ly like this:

"Yes, we are even more eager!" The Fourth Concubine, who was actually two years older, repeated抢声重一句; the Fifth Concubine continued滔滔to say:

"You know, Mr. Ronggui, when our commander had not yet made his fortune,驻紥in XX province and was a civil official│concurrent chairman, how pleasant we were! A monthly allowance of three or five thousand was not a problem; the comfort of food and clothing was beyond words. Even when he was demoted to brigade commander the year before last, it was still acceptable. Now it has been reduced to only fifty yuan of pocket money per month, which is simply useless for anything. After seeing a play, you can't play mahjong again. Recently, even our previous private savings have almost all been used up. Last month, the First Wife went to Hankou to inquire about the commander's news, and we were full of hope! As long as the commander's matter is successful, we don't care about being under her control or receiving her cold looks. It's just that there has been no news since she left. Speaking of the commander, he is still an outsider! As long as his pockets are full, he is still generous, and his requests are always granted. Is that right, Mr. Ronggui?"

"That's right, that's right, especially for you. Even when I used to ask the commander for money, thirty or fifty would often be in hand as soon as I spoke," Mr. Ronggui replied. The Second Concubine brought in the mahjong, and everyone gathered around. The atmosphere in the room suddenly changed immediately.

The XX commander was originally a beggar sleeping in a temple廊in XX county, XX province. In the summer of the thirteenth year, because he stole a pumpkin from Li Si of Zhangjiawan, the village head and security chief decided to drive him out of the area. He drifted to XX province to become a soldier. "The situation creates heroes." Relying on his lantern-sized courage, he quelled bandits and resisted rebels, always successfully. In less than two years, he rose from soldier... to platoon leader... to company commander. In the fifteenth year, he dispatched troops to XX, and the discipline was so strict. Seeing merit and rewarding it, he bravely took on the task of right-wing assault. Sure enough, he was invincible and victorious in every battle, and he quickly rose to the rank of commander. At that time, he thought, "I don't really understand revolution. It's better to save more money and secretly marry a few young wives." So the Second Concubine, Third Concubine... Sixth Concubine also entered the commander's mansion one after another. Later, the commander was ordered to concurrently serve as provincial chairman. He clearly held a position in both military and political affairs.

That was probably because he was, after all, a military man by origin and easily tempted. Two representatives sent by the XX military commander of a neighboring province told him that if he wanted great hope, he should defect. He listened and thought, "That's right. If I want great hope, I should..." So he raised the flag and betrayed反 XX. The facts are always unpredictable, and it completely collapsed. This was the matter of the eighteenth year.

Finally, enduring until June of the nineteenth year, he made many turns and obtained a position as an independent brigade commander,驻紥in the wealthy XX county, XX province. Once, the county party department published his embezzlement, and he was furious, killing three party committee members. As a result, he was stripped of his powers by the government again.

There were many opportunities this year. XX still looked upon him埀靑and called him to Hankou to wait. Before leaving, he told his concubines:

"I have been unlucky for two years. The mansion in XX city and the land in XX county have all been sold. Your expenses are really too high. How many months can the little bit of money saved in the bank last? Before I assume a new position, your expenses must also be slightly reduced. You don't have to worry about food and clothing. Each of you will receive fifty yuan of pocket money per month, which will be distributed by the First Wife. Listen up!"

Last month, the commander wired the First Wife to go to Hankou. It could be guessed that there was a seventy to eighty percent chance of a new position. As a result, the concubines all beamed with joy, and the Second Concubine even suggested having a lively mahjong game to celebrate the First Wife's departure. Moreover, the Sixth Concubine, who had been rejected by the commander, also asked someone to come to the door to seek forgiveness again.

The First Wife had been gone for more than a month with no news, which was enough to make the concubines feel disappointed to the eleventh degree. What's more, the commander suddenly sent back a servant, saying that the concubines should pawn their gold jewelry to raise one thousand yuan to run sports, which made the concubines feel the coming of misfortune.

The Silk Padded Jacket

— Yi Ping

Zhang Da Ma watched her son go to the factory with his hands in his sleeves and his shoulders shrugged. Thinking about herself sitting at home eating, but wearing a thin padded jacket, "Although Afu is my son, can I watch my son suffer from the cold?" Besides, he is in his twenties and knows that the family is poor. He has never spent the money he earned on women like Li's Xiao Ding. Originally, the Zhang family was also a well-off family, but it was all spent by his father. Thanks to Afu's filial piety, otherwise, my old life would be difficult to live. Zhang Da Ma thought of this and couldn't help but shed tears; while her son's cotton robe was locked in the pawnshop, and it would take four yuan to redeem it. Facing this difficult problem, Zhang Da Ma sat by the box in a daze.

Finally, she mustered the courage to turn over that box. She knew very well that there were only a few worthless rags inside, but life is always filled with endless hope│she hoped that she might accidentally discover a piece of clothing that was slightly valuable. Broken and old, they were simply unrecognizable as to whether they were tops or pants, filling the ground. Zhang Da Ma excitedly pulled a brand-new silk padded jacket from the bottom of the box, as if she was going crazy. It was made a month before Zhang Da Ye died. Zhang Da Ma was saddened by seeing this padded jacket, so she casually stuffed it there. Now, it had given her great hope.

"This padded jacket must have cost twenty-odd dollars when it was made, and it has only been worn once. It should be enough to pawn for a cotton robe for my son, or maybe even two dollars more to buy a catty of jujubes for my son to nourish him," Zhang Da Ma thought as she walked, carefully folding the padded jacket in a broken package.

She looked around like a thief. Seeing no pedestrians on the road, she quickly turned into the screen of the pawnshop. She lifted her head and handed up the package. The clerk casually flipped through it. "How much?" The voice always sounded like a judge questioning a criminal because they most disliked old and out-of-date clothes.

"Sir, five... yuan... please..." Zhang Da Ma was afraid of being scolded by the clerk if she asked for too much and unwilling to give up the silk padded jacket that had only been worn once if she asked for too little.

"Bah!" If Zhang Da Ma hadn't snatched it back quickly, the package would have been thrown on the ground.

"Sir, how about this?" Zhang Da Ma tremblingly took out the pawn ticket for the cotton robe and sent the padded jacket up at the same time. "Exchange them, sir."

The clerk saw clearly that the amount on the pawn ticket was three yuan and four jiao. "No, no!" He pushed the things on the high counter down again.

"Sir, that padded jacket is made of silk!"

"Don't want it!" He was clearly angry that she didn't know her stuff.

"Sir, how much is it worth?"

"One yuan and two jiao!"

"Sir, three yuan, please." Zhang Da Ma thought, "I still have a few mao of silver in my pocket, which should be enough to redeem the cotton robe."

The clerk didn't seem to have that much time and didn't pay any attention to her.

On the way home, Zhang Da Ma thought, "A poor man's silk padded jacket is so worthless!"

Novel

Sympathizer (Part 5)

— Zhang Henshui

His mother said: Isn't this as precious as gold? Now it's the hungry months in the countryside. Rice only sells for four yuan a dan. Eight yuan is two dan of rice? How can that be? Can we still afford to study! Meng Guobin was very unhappy when he heard his mother say this, and went into his room in anger. After entering the room, sure enough, the oil lamp was lit on the table, the teapot was cool, and a wisp of green smoke was rising upward in swirls under the table. By the table was a green bamboo chair, upright and clean, without a speck of dust. He thought to himself, "My family has treated me quite well. I often think that my family is a petty bourgeoisie. But if my family were not petty bourgeoisie, where would I get the money to study? I wouldn't even know what petty bourgeoisie is. However, people like my father are always stubborn in their thinking. I said that Wang Lao Er is an oppressed person, but he doesn't think so. He thinks it's good that he picked more than two dan of other people's crops and got half of the rice to eat. He doesn't think that that half is given to the absentee landlord, which is very unfair. My father's behavior can represent the opinions of small landlords, which is worth noting. Tomorrow, I can talk to Wang Lao Er and see what they think about the landlords." Thinking like this, he took out his sixteen-yuan fountain pen from his pocket, and also took out a diary, and wrote a line on it, saying: The landlord thinks that the land he bought with his assets is given to the tenants to cultivate, and the tenants should share half of the produce. As for the fact that he has not contributed the slightest effort to the cultivation, he does not ask. After this passage, he listed several questions in his diary, preparing to use them as materials for talking with Wang Lao Er tomorrow. He had been home for three days, and the work of investigating the rural economy should also begin. After formulating the questions, he flipped through several social science books he had brought back, making a theoretical reference, and then went to bed. Because he had used his brain too much, his nerves reacted, and when he went to bed, he dreamed of going to Wang Lao Er's house. Wang Er's wife brewed tea, fried melon seeds, and treated him with extra hospitality. The harvest he gained in his dream was actually much richer than when he was awake. The next day, when he woke up and looked at his watch, it was nine o'clock. But his family had already eaten breakfast. His eldest and second brothers had gone to the fields to watch people tread waterwheels, his eldest and second sisters-in-law were spinning麻in their respective rooms, his mother had taken two nieces to the vegetable garden to pick vegetables, and two nephews had gone to the village school to study. When the sun was high in the sky, the family was quiet. He got another feeling, thinking that although his family was a petty bourgeoisie, they were not a leisure class. There were probably very few leisure classes in the countryside. As he was thinking this, he didn't know how he had alarmed his family. So his eldest sister-in-law served tea and water, his second sister-in-law fried rice for him to eat, and his mother also got the news and took out two eggs from the藤簸籮basket on the bottom layer of the wardrobe and fried them for him as a dish. Meng Guobao certainly knew that his family was very hospitable to him, but this kind of hospitality was a bit excessive, and he felt that it made him feel uncomfortable. He ate his meal hastily, and looked at the sun, which was not far from the middle of the sky. This was what the country people called mid-morning, which was more reliable than a clock, so Meng Guobin didn't bother to look at his watch, but only looked at the shadow of the sun. At this time, it was time for his appointment with Wang Lao Er, so he straightened his clothes, smoothed his hair with his hand, and went to Wang Lao Er's house. Wang Lao Er口旱烟袋was watching at the gate. Seeing Meng Guobao coming, he bowed and said, "Mr. Meng is here, please come inside and sit down." (To be continued)

Little History of a Star

Little History of Gwili Andre

— Xie Nan

While we are vigorously opposing films that insult our nation, gold-dollar producers continue to shoot films depicting our people's ugliness such as拖瓣子, selling opium, and kidnapping, and promoting them on the international stage. What is introduced here is the female lead in "Roar of the Dragon," a film with a background similar to these.

Before圭利安特丽Gwili Andre, no one in the silver screen knew her, but in her homeland, Sweden, because her father was a famous writer and art designer, no one in Copenhagen did not know him, and no one did not know that he had a very beautiful daughter. She had excellent talent, but she loved to dress up and didn't like to study, often sneaking out and not coming back, so many tutors were unwilling to teach her anymore.

At the age of sixteen, she was already well-known in the local social circles; but at that time, she was still alone because she held the tenet that "a free soul is considered free." Her parents also approved of her idea and finally let her come to the free land of America.

In a certain village in America, she had a relative who had a very beautiful villa, so she went to live there. Within twenty-four hours of her arrival, many unfamiliar men came to visit her, but most were politely rejected. She just diligently practiced網球 and swimming at home. But after all, her beauty and liveliness, and the environment in America that had been熏洗for a long time, would not allow a hero to be buried forever, so she became famous in society in less than half a year after arriving in America. The RKO company heard of her fame and invited her to the screen, which was the first voice in the main film world.

Later, relying on her talent and hard work, she gradually attracted attention in Hollywood. Before long, her free soul had been bound (?); because she already had a loving partner, who was a handsome and unmarried young man in the area. The two often danced and swam together.

In addition to liking music, she also had a hobby of collecting Chinese porcelain and antiques. Recently, she also loved collecting shells, often going to remote and isolated islands with people in boats, and bringing back a lot of shells. In short, everything about her was very mysterious and eccentric, and she was indeed a typical U (Unknown) type of woman in Hollywood. But we do not want this U-character girl and李却迪克斯to meet us in this "Roar of the Dragon."

Editor's note: After the film "Roar of the Dragon" was released in the United States, the public opinion was extremely unfavorable. The content was superficial and bad, and the performance was naive and tasteless. The Americans have already made a conclusion. It probably won't come to our country to show itself. Please rest assured, readers.

Overseas Rare News

Movies in Taiwan

— Xing Su

Taiwan, which was seized by Japan, is a place of beautiful mountains and rivers. It is divided into six prefectures: Keelung, Taipei, Tainan, Taichung, Kaohsiung, and Hualien Port (which is Taitung). Now all prefectures have trains. Transportation is very convenient, and the market is gradually prospering. There are now more than twenty movie theaters operating, most of which were established by Japanese people, so most of the films shown are also Japanese productions. The layout of the movie theaters is completely Japanese-style, and the audience sits on the floor. The theaters employ specialists to read the description in the hall, but this custom is gradually being abolished. There are many overseas Chinese there, and they give a warm welcome to films produced by the motherland. According to statistics, since China has had its own films, more than two hundred kinds of films have been imported. The productions of the Mingxing and Tianyi companies are the most trusted. Other small organizations such as Youlian also import many of their productions. The productions of Lianhua Company do not seem to sell very well. The reason is that the folk customs in Taiwan are brave and there are fewer intellectuals, so they especially welcome martial arts films. There are four film vendors operating in Shanghai. The copyright fee for selling to Taiwan, calculated according to the two-year copyright period, is at least seven or eight hundred yuan for each silent film, and as much as one thousand two or three hundred yuan, depending on whether the film is popular with the audience there. It is a pity that the Chinese film industry does not seem to pay much attention to the copyright there. If the operation is improved, it would be an excellent market for promoting domestic films.

Publication News of Yinguang Monthly

The Yinguang Monthly, a publication of the United Film Company, is edited by Zhou Shoujuan and Zheng Shufang. All the pictures and texts are extremely refined. The picture part is printed by photogravure, which is even more exquisite. The first issue is being compiled and printed. Anyone who has a research interest in Western film art can contribute to the magazine. Whether it is original or translated, it is welcome. However, the style should be in vernacular with new punctuation marks. Once published, remuneration will be given accordingly. The address of the company is at the United Film Company, No. 384 North Suzhou Road, in this city.

Introduction to National Films

"Two Orphan Girls of the Battlefield"

"Two Orphan Girls of the Battlefield," which has been rumored in Shanghai for a long time, why is it silent again? People who care about domestic films must hope to know.

After it was filmed in September, it was once banned from public screening by the Central Film Inspection Association; later, after疏通, it finally received a passport. Unexpectedly, when it arrived in Shanghai, it was banned again by the authorities in the concession. Tianyi Company thought that since it could not be screened in the concession, and it was unwilling to screen it in small theaters outside the concession, the talk of the Shanghai premiere had to be shelved. But the Beijing-Suzhou area had already been shown!

The reporter went to Beijing last time and watched it at the Nanjing Grand Theater in the capital. So let's talk about it briefly.

The film is very long and the plot is very complicated: the general idea is: because of the Shanghai war, there was a weak girl whose family was destroyed. Her father died to save another girl. The two girls were separated before they could even ask each other's names. The rescued girl lived in her cousin's house and got engaged to her cousin. Good things are hard to come by. Her cousin fell in love with a female teacher. So she tried her best to make her cousin break off his love. Later, her cousin joined the army and met a nurse, who was actually an old lover (the female teacher). She also saw that the female teacher was the orphan girl whose father sacrificed for her; so she护gave her fiancé││cousin│　to her rival in love││benefactor││. She joined the women's battle team herself; but her rival in love was also unwilling to be the victor in a love triangle, so she continued to work as a frontline nurse.

The film introduces a newly successful male and female actor, Lu Lixia, who is also very competent, and the protagonist, Hu Shan, is the most moving. In Nanjing, many people criticized and said: She is even better than her sister││Hu Die││. I hope that in the near future, people in Shanghai will also be able to see this film. I think it is better than Tianyi's representative work "The Footprints in the Orchid Valley".

Film Monographs

The "Smile" That Everyone Can Do

— Chen Dabei

From the first to the fifth formula of the unique facial expression learning method, we have already practiced five of the most basic facial expressions. Although these five expressions also have various changes, they are relatively easy to practice, because they are very simple, and people of all statuses perform them similarly.

Now we want to go further and talk about practicing more complex and varied expressions. The first is the "smile" that everyone can do.

Indeed, there is no one who cannot smile. Even babies in their mother's arms can smile, so why is it necessary to practice? Little do people know that smiling is the most difficult expression to perform appropriately in the performing arts. Anyone with a little directing or acting experience knows this. When directing a scene of laughter, directors often encounter many difficulties. Because people of different statuses must produce different kinds of smiles. In daily life, we have light smiles, fake smiles, sneers, cold smiles, amusing smiles, flattering smiles, silly smiles, wild laughter, roaring laughter, and so on. When the director wants you to laugh out loud, you face the camera and give a forced smile, or when you are asked to perform a toothy smile, you can't help but burst into roaring laughter. Sometimes, you think you are smiling, but the shadow left on the film looks like you are crying. Such mistakes can often waste many feet of film and sacrifice the precious time of many colleagues. This is because you have not paid attention to your own smile at all times, and you have not practiced until you have sufficient confidence. The reason for this is that you usually despise this smile that everyone can do.
